<rate>5< /rate>< review>
I was obsessed with Tabu Shabu when i discovered it in Carlsbad, went back 3x on that mini getaway. There‚Äôs something about the freshness of eating shabu shabu (hot pot) that is so satisfying.

Then Tabu Shabu takes it an extra step, they transform your leftovers into an Asian Risotto... creamy, delicious, and mouth-wateringly good.

Service was great at this Huntington Harbour location in an outdoor mall by Trader Joe‚Äôs. They play upbeat music, keep the space sanitized and comfortable, they seat parties in pods, constant attention given with extra condiments, serving utensils, monitoring your broth, super hot sauce drops in your dipping sauce upon request, etc.

We got the grass fed prime beef regular size and tonkotsu broth or spicy miso / tonkotsu mix.

Bountiful set of fresh veggies that you can choose to customise, my daughter only got broccoli, spinach and tofu.

My teenage nephew inhaled his first round of beef, so we got him another set of beef..

It‚Äôs a lot of food, so i always have a lot of leftovers. They take your leftover broth, add rice, add more broth over and over until it thickens. Then add an egg and chilli garlic sauce and other yummy stuff, and sesame seeds.. omg.. it‚Äôs so good that i dream about eating it.

Highly recommend!<//review>

< text>
There is ONE thing I need from an inn, and that is a quiet night's rest in comfortable surroundings - and that is EXACTLY what Mayfair provided.

The inn is QUIET, partly because of the concrete building and partly because it is a smaller property (fewer rooms = less traffic, fewer neighbors, and less noise).  A quiet night's rest, perfect!

The rooms are tidy, the cleanliness was good, all rooms are non-smoking (no stale cigarette smell), and the views of the nearby mountains are impressive.  There's a TV, a fridge/freezer, microwave.  Truly comfortable and I'd stay again.< /text>

<text>Unfortunately, we had an experience that felt genuine at the beginning, but ended up being a disappointing one. We called an electrician at Point Loma Electric & Plumbing because our electricity was down in half the house. Although we had an older panel, our wires were recently installed, but the electrician did not explain that until after the service. He could have been honest and told us the needed service (changing a breaker) versus the $2,500 service to change a panel and make sure they weren‚Äôt double tapped (no new wires).<//text><pictures>None</pictures><response>{'time': 1611854648753, 'text': "We are very sorry to learn you are feeling this way.  After reviewing your invoice, job photos and the technicians notes I can confirm that you had a Zinsco panel that was in poor condition with double tapped breakers.  Double tapped means that multiple wires are placed on a single circuit breaker rather than individual circuits each on their own breaker.  Zinsco panels are considered hazardous and lost their UL listing over 30 years ago and absolutely should be replaced.  We will always recommend replacement of the panel and not just a breaker under these circumstances. The electrician did discuss this with you and explained the scope of work and cost; according to our records you agreed to the work being done.  He then completed the job exactly as explained and agreed. There is far more involved than simply the cost of a panel and this pricing is in line with what other comparable companies charge for this scope of work.  All breakers were also replaced and the wires were properly re-landed in the new panel.  The wires do not need to be replaced unless they are in poor condition (and that would cost more) and there is no reason to re route them.  I apologize if the scope of work wasn't explained to your complete understanding, however the work was done as  necessary and as agreed and was indeed needed.  Your technician and our company take great pride in our integrity and workmanship and would not recommend or charge for work unless it was needed and approved.\nPlease feel free to reach out to me directly if you have additional questions or would like further explanation.\nSincerely,\nJamie Hunley\nOwner, Point Loma Electric & Plumbing"}<//response>< gmapID>

If you are like me and are fearful, or smart, and not into electrocuting yourself doing home projects then this is the business to call. James and his associate came out for an evaluation, he gave me multiple avenues to approach the issue and at a price that I felt was reasonable.

Issue: Breaker blew, lost power to multiple areas of the house. Had too much power on one breaker.
